<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< text>
My experience with Rolloface has been awesome.  I purchased my brake kit from Rolloface because I was able to save a little money compared to purchasing the same kind of kit from Brembo or Wilwood.  Also this kit weighs half as much as the OEM setup I replaced. When you have a heavy car like a Challenger,  this kit being lighter was a definate plus.

The Rolloface team really looks out for the customer.
After I chose my brake kit and sent payment,  they actually refunded me some money cause they had to put a smaller size rotor in the kit for the rear.  Turns out the kit i had purchased had a rotor  size that would have put too much brake bias on the rear. If that's not looking out for a customers best interest I don't know what is.

Ive had the kit installed on my car for over 2 years now and still working great.  The customer service I have recieved has been phenomenal.  Ken went over and above in dealing with the logistics of getting my brake kit to me in the midst of a major event weekend.  The ordering process was awesome in the way you get to choose from any color imaginable unlike other companies that only have a handful of color offerings.  The after the sale service and support is great too.  During one of my spirited driving moments one of my calipers got damaged. The brake caliper  held up like a tank  but  some debris that got  up under my car took a chunk out from the corner  of it.  It was only cosmetic damage but I was able to order up another caliper and Rolloface was able to build it and get it out to me in record time for my next event.  I can honestly say too that the performance of these brakes is unbelievable.  For as heavy as my car is, they will stop the car quick.  Saved me from getting caught up in a collision that happened right in front of me.

The only issue I have is that dang air freshener that came with the kit didn't last very long lol.</text>

My V8 Absolute was dropped right out of the box, breaking the cyclone section of the wireless stick vacuum. I never even had the chance to use it before I broke it. I could not even blame someone else as a scape goat.

The technician brought the replacement part into his service center from another location, overnight trying to get me my unit back to me as quickly as possible. Although, these great efforts to return me my unit, the vacuum was not functioning per their standard for my model.   He then replaced the canister. Trying to put it into service he then realized that my battery was not taking a charge nor holding a charge either. He replaced the battery pack. Now, this was the third component that had faultered. However, there was "NO CHARGE" for any of the repairs. I was "floored" to say the least. I told him that I dropped this unit to the floor when it broke.

Location and prices are good. There is a 24-hour open diner just in front of the hotel (Denny's), and also there is a 7-eleven market nearby. The light rail is very close and you may use it to go to downtown easily. Beds are comfortable, and the staff is cheerful.

<rating>5<//rating>< username>
Alexander Houston<//username>
< Review>
Great value for the price. Little pricier than others (not much though!) but it's only a couple mins to Uber (or walk) to/from the airport. I needed a new key, and the guy at the desk was very helpful and friendly about it. I needed to extend my stay at the last minute and they were accommodating. They even brought new (warm!) towels and soap to us later that day. No comments about the other staff like the cleaning service, as we did not use those services. They share a parking lot with Denny's which is convenient. Who travels to California and eats at Denny's though?! Take the $40 to a seafood joint, or mexican! I think they have breakfast included too. It's more of a "go to the desk get a bagel and coffee and walk back to your room" kind of deal. Not much room for more than a couple people at once. That's fine but your room could be across the whole parking lot which isn't always worth it. No comment about the food itself as I didn't get the breakfast. Would recommend. No complaints, especially for the price and location.< /Review>

<Rating>1<//Rating><Review>I was so disappointed to hear how poorly the receptionist at the Vagabond Hotel has treated my sister. My sister and brother-in-law took a trip to the east coast, and they planned on staying at the Vagabond when they flew back to California, because their home is several hours away from the airport.

But when 2 family members on the east coast passed away in a span of 24 hours, my sister had to change her travel plans at the last minute. The deadlines for reservation cancellations had already passed, but the airlines and other hotels involved showed some compassion to my family and made an exception for my sister's difficult circumstances. Everyone helped her cancel and/or reschedule reservations so she could attend two funerals last week -- everyone EXCEPT the receptionist at the Vagabond Hotel. The woman with the Indian accent -- who refused to share her name, so I'm calling her the "receptionist" -- was rude to my sister, charged her for a room that wasn't used, refused to consult her supervisor about a better solution, and then refused to speak any further with my sister.

When I called the hotel, on behalf of my sister, to try to get some information about what was happening, the woman hung up on me.

<Rating>4<//Rating>< Review>
You might think Sushi in Del Mar is gonna be a costly endeavor and that you might be able to save some time and money by going a little further north to Solana, Encinitas or Carlsbad and in general you'd be right, but this unassuming spot barely looks like a sushi spot from the outside and actually that rusty gate from the grocery store next door probably scare people off. It's awesome to come here when it's slow, you get super fast and amazing food and during daytime they have a HH that's killer on the deals. Kai roll, sushi burrito, philly.

They serve a ton of regulars and most of the staff will remember you if you come in a lot. The service is great, but most of all from the chef's with their great flavor profiles, knife skills and recommendations.

They have some major price jumps between standard rolls and premium as well as for their MP items like Uni, Toro, etc. The salad pricing like wakame is a bit high. If you don't mind getting certain rolls the HH can be as inexpensive as any place around, but their quality will keep you coming back regardless of the price.

Found out about this place as they also own Nozomi in Carlsbad, another diamond in the rough. Urban, Balance and Flower Hill have brought a lot more attention to this side of the 5.

Their salmon tends to be firm, while their tuna I found soft. They use a lot of jalapeno, cream cheese and sriracha in their rolls. They perfectly don't over fry their shrimp, the unagi sauce is a bit of an overload and really sweet. I always ask to go easy on the crunchies if any at all.

I don't like the word fusion and you'll see it in the rest of their menu being that it's pretty limited on the back end, but the front chefs are great.<//Review>

< text>
My wife and I ordered teriyaki vegetables and sushi to-go and were relatively disappointed with our meal. The service we experienced was good and we received our to-go order quickly, but the sushi just wasn't that great. The teriyaki vegetables were amazing and we really enjoyed those, but the two sushi rolls we ordered were just mediocre. Part of our issue was that the soy sauce which was served with our sushi (in little to-go packets) was incredibly salty. Disgustingly so. It completely overwhelmed the flavor of the sushi, the ginger, and the wasabi sauce. We'll definitely be back for some more teriyaki vegetables and chicken, but next time we'll probably skip the sushi. On a side note the prices for a $$ location weren't too bad. You can purchase sushi rolls there for as low as $5.50-ish (for an 8-piece roll). More expensive rolls can run up to $15 for a 10 piece roll. The excellent teriyaki vegetables were $12 for a substantial serving.</text>

< Text>
When I went to pick-up my "Otis" rug (for over $800) from the San Francisco store, I was told to load it into the car myself as the warehouse staff would not help.  I should have known then that the customer service at EQ3 is non-existent.

It shed quite a bit in the beginning which I attributed to it being new and assumed it would eventually subside.  Unfortunately, this poor quality rug sheds INCESSANTLY and I have to vacuum our hardwood floors daily to clean-up all of the threads.

I brought this to the attention of the store manager and he informed me that it was not his problem and that I would have to contact customer service in Winnipeg, Canada.  For this reason alone the company deserves only one star, but that is only the beginning.

I spoke with Victoria Knapp in the customer service department and she asked me to explain the problem and send photos.  This was followed-up by multiple email exchanges and Victoria explaining that it is "normal" for a rug to shed incessantly.

I was then put in contact with Ryan Franz, EQ3 Customer Care Team Lead.  Mr. Franz also informed me that it was customary for this rug to shed excessively.

Well . . . that was two years ago and I still have to vacuum the floor every day to clean-up this mess of a rug.

EQ3 has some cool stuff but the workmanship is shoddy and the customer service is non-existent.   Save your money and frustration!  There are plenty of other business with better products and better customer service.< /Text>
